{"id": 794476, "created_at": "2017-06-13T15:56:04Z", "subject": "Tinycards and Duolingo Integration?", "description": "I've been using Tinycards to boost my learning of German and I want to start by saying that it's a great tool. It offers lots of back and forth translation and is as especially good way to drill which noun takes which article (der/die/das). The structure of the deck also coordinates nicely with the structure of the Duolingo course (obviously) which is great. But that has made me wonder why these offerings aren't even further integrated.\r\nWhy not, for example, have a hyperlink to the Tinycards Deck (or the matching lesson within the deck) right from the relevant language course or lesson on the Duolingo page (or app)? And vice-versa, a link to the Duolingo lesson from the Tinycard deck?\r\n\r\nIn fact, since one frequent complaint from users is that Duolingo tends to throw words into a lesson before the user has been really introduced to them, why not automatically start with a flashcard session before each new lesson is run for the first time? I think a lot of users would appreciate that, although users could (probably should) be offered the chance to skip the flashcard session if they'd prefer.\r\nWhy not coordinate their decay rates so that specific card sub-decks and Duolingo tree skill modules go 'stale' at the same time? Currently all sub-decks go a little bit stale every day (from what I can tell) whereas lessons use the smart algorithm to determine when it's time to review which skills. If they were linked, both would work off of the same set of weak words, and reviewing either one (the lesson or the deck) would bring the other back to full strength.\r\n\r\nWhy not let a person earn at least some Duolingo XP for reviewing or learning a set of Tinycard flash cards? The cards are an awesome tool, but at present one's Duolingo skill-level (XP/Fluency) does not reflect any time spent reviewing the cards.\r\nI think there's a real opportunity here for the developers, and I'd really love to hear from an Admin: are there currently any plans to pursue integration like this? ", "category_labels": []}

{"id": 795575, "created_at": "2017-06-15T03:27:18Z", "subject": "Various suggestions", "description": "Bug: I deselected to share my email in Facebook when logging into Tinycards for the first time on my computer. So when I try to login to Tinycards using Facebook, it now just refreshes the login page instead of giving any sort of error. (I had previously logged in on iOS and it automatically recognized me.) I expected that the email wouldn't be required or that it would \"just work\" since Duo has access to the same core Bio info and I was already logged into Duo. \u00af\\_(\u30c4)_/\u00af Since I've identified the problem, I'll go fix it on my end eventually. It would just be nice if it weren't an issue to begin with and it might confuse other people :)\r\n\r\nSuggestion: some sort of setting or auto-detect so I don't have to type really long answers. I like doing recall for shorter words, but something like \"dotted sixteenth note\" is a little long, especially for my slow tapping.\r\n\r\nSuggestion: allow multiple correct answers. The music symbols deck I tried out had \"Forte (strong)\" and would not accept just \"Forte\", it needed \"forte strong\". I think either answer should have been acceptable and it should be easy for the deck maker to mark that without necessarily showing all valid variants to the user. Also, if the word \"note\" at the end of those answers could be visible but greyed out once you start typing so you know that it is optional (when it hopefully is), that would be great!\r\n\r\nFun Suggestion: The element K is Kalium. I guess the modern name is potassium, but I want the old name accepted too!!!! :)\r\n\r\nSuggestion: Formula-based cards? This is is probably too specific to be considered, but maybe it could be generalized. On the Cyrillic letters card set, there are a few cards that represent example words instead of individual letters. It would be nice if the words could be randomly generated from a list, so there is more variety. This is a little bit against the purpose of flashcards, but I think it works for letters. As an alternative, maybe the deck could have multiple parts, so only 3-letter words are shown as possible solutions to 3-letter cards. If the deck were split like that, there would probably need to be a setting (frequency adjustment) or meta-data (e.g. keep track of incorrectly transposed letters within the word) to keep the focus on knowing the letters, not the words. Maybe the words could be split off into sideboards/extensions that are default enabled while unlocking the deck, but can be turned off/down later? I like the word-cards, but I feel like they need an extra feature of some sort to really make them feel like they belong.\r\n\r\nSuggestion: large info cards. Cards that are larger than a typical card and are just for information purposes when unlocking the deck, and live in a review tab separate from normal cards. These cards would describe something larger than a regular card such as zooming in on the map of China and labeling a bunch of provinces near each other, or showing multiple adjacent layers of the earth or parts of an eye, or even just a collection of verbs related to talking. Not every deck would need these, but they would help provide a broader context. It would require the deck maker to add extra meta-data, but these cards could show up as review if I keep confusing two adjacent provinces that are on the same overview card. Maybe these could be integrated as an optional unit-for-unlocking-a-deck?\r\n\r\nSuggestion: I'd prefer not to be asked if I remember something when doing the strength/practice mode. I hope these become less frequent over time and would rather just be given the flash card, even multiple times (in different question types), over these. I don't really like the review cards either, but they seem to only appear when I'm having trouble and they're actually helpful. This might just be personal preference, but these sorts of cards take me out of the flow.\r\n\r\nSuggestion: be able to select a set of decks, or even just all favorites that have been started, and play with all the decks at once. For the three-cards format, all three cards would be from the answer's deck.\r\n\r\nNitpick: On \"Deck Settings\" in iPad iOS, the X and trash are horizontally indented from the edge less than I would expect. Also, I didn't have confidence that the x would save my changes, though I'm not sure a checkmark would be better. Since there isn't a cancel button anyways, it would be nice to be able to tap off the modal to close it.\r\n\r\nThanks for making the app, it has already has some great content in it!", "category_labels": []}

You will see the options to add a cover photo for your deck, title and description. To your right you will see a (+) sign on a blue background, that allows you to create cards.\n\n\nInstruction on how to delete a deck:\n\nYou can select on the Me tab and select on the deck you wish to delete. You will see a pencil icon which is edit, select that and you will see settings. {"id": 798956, "created_at": "2017-06-19T23:56:09Z", "subject": "Tinycards Web Feedback", "description": "It would be useful to be able to reverse which side of the card you see first, i.e., whether you see foreign language side first (on the face card side) or the English  first. Since textbooks tend to give the foreign language first and the English definition second, the one tends to enter the face card side with the foreign language and the flip side with English. For me, it would be more useful to be shown the English word first (on the face side of the card) and the foreign language on the flip side. It's tougher, and maybe a better learning experience, to have to come up with the foreign word that matches the English, rather than the other way around. This is especially true with foreign languages that have congates that make it somewhat easy to guess the English meaning. I solved this problem by re-entering two decks of cards, putting the English on the face side and the foreign language on the flip side. The work was tedious. It would have been helpful to have had a feature that truly let me flip the card priority from the foreign language first, to English first. Also, instructions on \"how to use the program\" might have helped me out, explaining to enter the English on the face side and the foreign language on the flip side for a \"better\" learning experience.\n\nUser Agent: Mozilla/5.0 (Windows NT 10.0; Win64; x64) AppleWebKit/537.36 (KHTML, like Gecko) Chrome/58.0.3029.110 Safari/537.36", "category_labels": []}
